{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01DuiBP6zDqHUiBNDDQcuKbA","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01Qt1Zk4oMGWfPwCLWdm4r8X","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nEnvoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is a sophisticated subsystem that coordinates the processing of HTTP requests from downstream clients, through a configurable filter chain, to upstream services. This document explains the architecture, data flow, and interaction patterns between the key components that make up this system.\n\nThe HCM operates at the network layer (as a `Network::ReadFilter`) and is protocol-agnostic—it transparently handles HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, and HTTP/3 through pluggable codec implementations. The request processing follows a well-defined pipeline: connection establishment → codec instantiation → per-stream filter chain execution → route selection → upstream forwarding.\n\n---\n\n## Component Responsibilities\n\n### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl\n\n**Location:** `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` and `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n\nConnectionManagerImpl is the central network filter that owns the lifecycle of an HTTP connection. It serves multiple interfaces simultaneously:\n\n- **Network::ReadFilter**: Receives raw bytes from the network\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks**: Creates new streams when the codec detects incoming requests\n- **Network::ConnectionCallbacks**: Handles connection-level events (connect, disconnect, watermarks)\n- **Http::ApiListener**: Allows programmatic creation of streams (used by gRPC transcoding, async clients)\n\n#### Codec Instantiation\n\nThe codec is created lazily:\n- For **H1/H2**: The codec is instantiated on the first `onData()` call via the `createCodec()` method, examining the incoming bytes to determine the protocol\n- For **H3**: The codec is created during `onNewConnection()` since the QUIC transport has already been established\n- The codec implements `ServerConnection`, which calls back to `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` when requests arrive\n\n#### Stream Management\n\nEach incoming HTTP request is wrapped in an `ActiveStream` structure, which:\n- Owns a `FilterManager` instance (the per-stream filter chain executor)\n- Tracks request/response headers, trailers, and stream state\n- Implements codec callbacks for low-level protocol events\n- Maintains `StreamInfo` for tracing, access logging, and runtime statistics\n- Is stored in a linked list (`LinkedObject<ActiveStream>`) for efficient iteration during shutdown\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : LinkedObject<ActiveStream>,\n                      public Event::DeferredDeletable,\n                      public StreamCallbacks,\n                      public CodecEventCallbacks,\n                      public RequestDecoder {\n  FilterManager filter_manager_;\n  RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr request_headers_;\n  ResponseHeaderMapPtr response_headers_;\n  ResponseTrailerMapPtr response_trailers_;\n  uint64_t stream_id_;\n  // ... additional state fields\n};\n```\n\n#### Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Drain Management**: When a drain decision is signaled (typically during graceful shutdown), the connection manager:\n1. Sets the codec to drain mode\n2. Stops accepting new requests\n3. Allows in-flight requests to complete\n4. Closes the connection after all streams are finished\n\n**Overload Management**: Integrates with the overload manager to:\n- Detect resource exhaustion (CPU, memory, connection saturation)\n- Send 503 Service Unavailable responses when overload thresholds are exceeded\n- Trigger connection draining under severe conditions\n\n**Watermark-Based Flow Control**:\n- Monitors the underlying connection's write buffer via `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` and `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`\n- Propagates watermark events to all active streams\n- Each stream notifies its filters to enable/disable reading from the request body\n\n---\n\n### 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain\n\n**Location:** `source/common/http/filter_manager.h` and `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n\nThe FilterManager is the per-stream execution engine for the HTTP filter chain. It orchestrates the passage of request headers, body data, and trailers through a chain of filters.\n\n#### Filter Chain Structure\n\nThe filter chain is asymmetric:\n\n**Decoder Filters (Request Path)**: Execute in configured order (A → B → C)\n- Receive `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `decodeTrailers()`, `decodeMetadata()`\n- May stop iteration, buffer data, or modify headers\n- Responsible for forwarding to the next filter or local reply\n\n**Encoder Filters (Response Path)**: Execute in reverse order (C → B → A)\n- Receive `encode1xxHeaders()`, `encodeHeaders()`, `encodeData()`, `encodeTrailers()`, `encodeMetadata()`\n- Allow modification of response headers before sending to the client\n- This reverse order allows filters to apply transformations symmetrically\n\n```cpp\n// Decoder filters: forward iteration\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.begin(); }\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.end(); }\n};\n\n// Encoder filters: reverse iteration\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.rbegin(); }  // reverse begin\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.rend(); }      // reverse end\n};\n```\n\n#### Filter Lifecycle and Iteration Control\n\nEach filter wrapper (ActiveStreamDecoderFilter/ActiveStreamEncoderFilter) manages iteration state:\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStreamFilterBase {\n  enum class IterationState {\n    Continue,        // Continue to next filter\n    StopIteration,   // Stop, but continue processing later events\n    StopAllIteration // Buffer data, stop processing until conditions change\n  };\n\n  bool commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback(FilterHeadersStatus status, bool& end_stream);\n  bool commonHandleAfterDataCallback(FilterDataStatus status, Buffer::Instance& provided_data,\n                                     bool& buffer_was_streaming);\n};\n```\n\nWhen a filter returns:\n- **FilterHeadersStatus::Continue**: The next filter is invoked immediately\n- **FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration**: Iteration halts; the filter must explicitly call `continueDecoding()` or `continueEncoding()`\n- **FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIteration**: In addition to stopping iteration, data buffering is enabled\n\n#### Filter Chain Factory\n\nThe `FilterChainFactory` interface allows configuration of which filters are instantiated for each stream:\n\n```cpp\nclass FilterChainFactory {\npublic:\n  virtual void createFilterChain(FilterChainManager& manager) PURE;\n};\n```\n\nAt stream creation, the factory is invoked with the FilterManager to install decoder/encoder filters in the appropriate order. Filters are instantiated in order and may be:\n- **Decoder-only**: Implement `StreamDecoderFilter`\n- **Encoder-only**: Implement `StreamEncoderFilter`\n- **Dual filters**: Implement `StreamFilter` (both decoder and encoder)\n\n#### Local Reply Mechanism\n\nIf a filter (or any upstream component) detects an error, it can issue a local reply:\n\n```cpp\nfilter_manager_.sendLocalReply(\n  Http::Code::BadRequest,\n  \"Invalid header\",\n  [](ResponseHeaderMap& headers) { /* modify headers */ },\n  absl::nullopt,  // grpc_status\n  \"filter_validation_failed\"\n);\n```\n\nThe FilterManager:\n1. Stops further filter iteration\n2. Creates response headers (with the provided status code)\n3. Invokes encoder filters in reverse order\n4. Sends the response directly to the downstream codec\n5. Resets the stream\n\n---\n\n### 3. Router Filter\n\n**Location:** `source/common/router/router.h` and `source/common/router/router.cc`\n\nThe router filter is the **terminal decoder filter** in the standard HCM filter chain. Its responsibility is to:\n1. Select a route based on request properties\n2. Determine the target cluster/upstream service\n3. Create an `UpstreamRequest` and forward the request to the cluster manager\n4. Handle retries, timeouts, and upstream response processing\n\n#### Route Selection\n\nThe router uses the `RouteConfiguration` (obtained from the route provider) to match the incoming request:\n\n```cpp\n// From router_filter_interface.h\nclass Router {\n  virtual void setRoute(Router::RouteConstSharedPtr route) override {\n    // Cache the selected route\n  }\n};\n```\n\nRoute matching considers:\n- **Virtual hosts**: Hostname-based grouping of routes (from `:authority` header or SNI)\n- **Routes**: Ordered list of route entries matched by:\n  - Path prefix/regex\n  - Methods (GET, POST, etc.)\n  - Headers and header patterns\n  - Query parameters\n  - Traffic policy (canary, shadow)\n\nOnce a route is selected, the router extracts the **cluster name** from the route entry and queries the `ClusterManager` for an HTTP connection pool.\n\n#### Upstream Request Lifecycle\n\nWhen a route is selected, the router creates an `UpstreamRequest`:\n\n```cpp\nclass UpstreamRequest : public GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks,\n                        public UpstreamToDownstreamImplBase {\n  void acceptHeadersFromRouter(bool end_stream);\n  void acceptDataFromRouter(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n  void onPoolReady(std::unique_ptr<GenericUpstream>&& upstream,\n                   Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host,\n                   const Network::ConnectionInfoProvider& address_provider,\n                   StreamInfo::StreamInfo& info,\n                   absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol) override;\n};\n```\n\nThe flow:\n\n1. **Request Pools**: The router calls `cluster_manager_->getPool()` passing:\n   - Cluster name\n   - Load balancing context (for host selection)\n   - Protocol preferences (H1, H2, H3)\n\n2. **Pool Acquisition**: The ClusterManager returns a connection pool. If no connection is available:\n   - **Pool Pending**: The UpstreamRequest's `onPoolReady()` callback is invoked once a connection is obtained\n   - **Pool Failure**: `onPoolFailure()` is invoked; the router issues a local reply with 503 or 504\n\n3. **Request Forwarding**: Once `onPoolReady()` is called with an upstream connection:\n   - An `UpstreamCodecFilter` is instantiated within an `UpstreamFilterManager`\n   - Request headers/body/trailers are forwarded to the upstream codec\n   - The upstream codec encodes and sends the request on the wire\n\n4. **Response Reception**: The upstream codec decodes response bytes and invokes:\n   - `decodeHeaders()`: Response status and headers\n   - `decodeData()`: Response body chunks\n   - `decodeTrailers()`: Optional trailers\n   - These flow backwards through the encoder filter chain to the downstream encoder\n\n#### Retry Logic\n\nThe router implements sophisticated retry handling via `RetryStateImpl`:\n\n```cpp\nclass RetryStateImpl {\n  void onUpstreamReset(Upstream::UpstreamResetReason reason);\n  bool shouldRetry(absl::optional<Http::Code> code, bool reset_reason_is_timeout);\n};\n```\n\nRetries are triggered by:\n- **Connection failures**: Pool timeout, connection refused, connection reset\n- **Specific response codes**: 5xx errors (configurable via retry policies)\n- **Timeout**: Per-try timeout exceeded\n\nConfiguration specifies:\n- Maximum retry count\n- Backoff policy (exponential with jitter)\n- Retriable response codes\n- Host selection strategy (use same host, alternate host)\n\n#### Timeout Management\n\nThe router maintains two timeout levels:\n\n- **Request timeout**: Total time allowed for the request (including retries)\n- **Per-try timeout**: Time limit for each individual attempt\n\nThese are set via:\n- Route configuration\n- `x-envoy-upstream-rq-timeout-ms` request header\n- `x-envoy-upstream-rq-per-try-timeout-ms` header\n\nWhen a timeout occurs:\n1. The current upstream request is reset\n2. If retries remain, a new attempt is initiated\n3. Otherwise, a 504 response is sent\n\n#### Hedged Requests (Per-Try Timeout)\n\nIf enabled, the router can initiate a secondary request before the primary completes:\n\n```cpp\n// When per_try_timeout triggers before the full request timeout:\n// 1. A new upstream request is started\n// 2. The first response to complete is used\n// 3. The slower request is abandoned\n```\n\n#### Shadow Routing\n\nThe router supports shadowing requests to a shadow cluster for testing:\n\n```cpp\nif (FilterUtility::shouldShadow(shadow_policy, runtime, stable_random)) {\n  auto shadow_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(...);\n  shadow_request->acceptHeadersFromRouter(end_stream);\n  // Response is silently discarded; no feedback to client\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n**Location:** `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h` and related files\n\nThe ClusterManager is the upstream connection pool and cluster management layer. It:\n1. Owns a registry of Cluster objects (one per configured cluster)\n2. Provides HTTP and TCP connection pools for each cluster\n3. Coordinates health checking and outlier detection\n4. Implements load balancing across hosts within a cluster\n\n#### ClusterManager Structure\n\n```cpp\nclass ClusterManagerImpl : public ClusterManager {\n  Cluster& cluster(const std::string& name);\n  Http::ConnectionPool::InstancePtr\n  getHttpConnectionPool(const ClusterConnectivityState& state,\n                        LoadBalancerContext* lb_context);\n};\n```\n\nEach `Cluster` object encapsulates:\n- A set of hosts/endpoints\n- A load balancer factory\n- Health checking configuration\n- Outlier detection rules\n- Circuit breaker limits\n\n#### Connection Pool Mechanics\n\nWhen the router requests a connection pool, the flow is:\n\n```\nRouter::getPool(cluster_name, load_balancing_context)\n  ↓\nClusterManager::getPool()\n  ↓\nCluster::getConnPool(dispatcher, load_balancer_context)\n  ↓\nConnectionPoolGrid::getPool()  [per-protocol instance]\n  ↓\nConnPoolBase::getHTTP1Connection() [if HTTP/1 pool requested]\n  ↓\n{\n  if (connection available and idle) {\n    return existing connection\n  } else if (connection limit not reached) {\n    create new connection and return\n  } else {\n    queue pending request\n  }\n}\n```\n\nA connection pool manages:\n- **Active connections**: Connections with in-flight requests\n- **Idle connections**: Connections available for reuse\n- **Pending requests**: Requests waiting for an available connection\n- **Watermark buffers**: Per-connection write buffers with high/low water marks\n\n#### Host Selection (Load Balancing)\n\nThe load balancer selects a specific host (endpoint) for each request:\n\n```cpp\nclass LoadBalancer {\n  HostConstSharedPtr chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext* context);\n};\n```\n\nThe router provides a `LoadBalancerContext` containing:\n- Request metadata (headers, cookies, etc.) for hash-based selection\n- Current retry count (for retry host selection)\n- Upstream zone information (for zone-aware routing)\n\nLoad balancing algorithms include:\n- **Round Robin**: Distribute evenly across healthy hosts\n- **Least Connections**: Select the host with fewest active connections\n- **Ring Hash**: Consistent hashing for session affinity\n- **Random**: Random selection\n- **Maglev**: Fast, deterministic hash with minimal disruption on host changes\n- **Locality-aware**: Prefer hosts in the same zone/region as the client\n\n#### Health Checking and Outlier Detection\n\n**Health Checking**: Periodic health checks (HTTP, TCP, gRPC) are configured per cluster:\n- Determines which hosts are available for traffic\n- Failed hosts are marked as unhealthy and excluded from load balancing\n- Recovered hosts are re-enabled\n\n**Outlier Detection**: Monitors request failures at runtime:\n- Tracks failure rates per host\n- Ejects hosts that exceed failure thresholds (e.g., >50% failure rate over 10 requests)\n- Periodically attempts to re-include ejected hosts\n- Provides fast, adaptive failure response (complementing health checks)\n\nBoth feed into the load balancer's host selection, ensuring traffic only reaches healthy hosts.\n\n#### Dynamic Cluster Discovery (CDS)\n\nClusters can be discovered dynamically via Cluster Discovery Service (CDS):\n\n```cpp\nclass CdsApi : public Config::SubscriptionCallbacks {\n  void onConfigUpdate(const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<ProtobufWkt::Any>& resources) override;\n};\n```\n\nCDS allows:\n- Adding new clusters without restarting\n- Updating cluster configuration (endpoints, health check policies)\n- Removing clusters gracefully\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Request Processing Pipeline\n\n### Downstream Request Path (Request Arrival to Upstream Dispatch)\n\n```\n1. Network Layer: Bytes arrive on downstream socket\n   └─→ ConnectionManager::onData(Buffer& data, bool end_stream)\n\n2. Codec Instantiation (first onData() call only)\n   └─→ ConnectionManager::createCodec()\n   └─→ HTTP1/2/3 CodecImpl selected\n   └─→ Codec parses protocol framing\n\n3. Stream Creation: Codec detects request headers\n   └─→ Codec::ServerConnection::newStream() callback\n   └─→ ConnectionManager::newStream(ResponseEncoder& response_encoder)\n   └─→ Creates ActiveStream with FilterManager\n\n4. Request Decoding: Codec delivers framing events\n   └─→ ActiveStream::decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream)\n   └─→ FilterManager::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n\n5. Filter Chain Execution (Decoder Path): A → B → C\n   ├─→ FilterA::decodeHeaders() → returns Continue\n   ├─→ FilterB::decodeHeaders() → returns Continue\n   ├─→ RouterFilter::decodeHeaders()\n   │   ├─→ Route selection (virtual host + route matching)\n   │   ├─→ Cluster selection from route\n   │   └─→ ClusterManager::getPool(cluster_name, lb_context)\n   │\n   └─→ Pool resolution callback invoked (synchronous or deferred)\n       ├─→ Host selection via load balancer\n       ├─→ Connection pool creates/reuses connection to host\n       └─→ UpstreamRequest created\n\n6. Body Data Processing: If request has body\n   └─→ ActiveStream::decodeData(Buffer& data, bool end_stream)\n   └─→ FilterManager::decodeData(data, end_stream)\n   └─→ Filters iterate in order (A → B → Router)\n   └─→ Router accumulates or forwards to upstream via UpstreamRequest\n\n7. Trailers Processing: If request has trailers\n   └─→ ActiveStream::decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMap& trailers)\n   └─→ FilterManager::decodeTrailers(trailers)\n   └─→ Filters iterate in order\n   └─→ Router forwards to upstream\n\n8. Upstream Request Forwarding (UpstreamRequest)\n   └─→ UpstreamCodecFilter encodes headers/data/trailers\n   └─→ Codec writes to upstream connection\n   └─→ Request transmitted on wire\n```\n\n### Upstream Response Path (Response Reception to Downstream Delivery)\n\n```\n1. Upstream Response: Bytes received on upstream socket\n   └─→ Upstream codec parses HTTP framing\n\n2. Response Decoding: Codec detects response headers\n   └─→ Codec::ResponseDecoder::decode1xxHeaders() / decodeHeaders()\n   └─→ UpstreamCodecFilter receives via CodecBridge\n   └─→ UpstreamFilterManager::encodeHeaders() [confusingly named]\n\n3. Upstream Filter Chain: Encoder filters (reverse order C → B → A)\n   └─→ Allow modification of response before sending to client\n\n4. Response Delivery to Router Filter\n   └─→ UpstreamRequest::decode1xxHeaders() / decodeHeaders() [legacy API]\n   └─→ Router notifies downstream filter chain via\n       RouterFilterInterface::onUpstream1xxHeaders() / onUpstreamHeaders()\n\n5. Response Encoding: Router injects response into downstream encoder chain\n   └─→ FilterManager::encodeHeaders() [actual encoding operation]\n   └─→ Encoder filters iterate in reverse (C → B → A)\n   └─→ Each filter may modify response headers\n\n6. Codec Encoding: Final encoder (ConnectionManager's codec)\n   └─→ ActiveStream::encodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream)\n   └─→ Codec encodes headers into wire format\n\n7. Response Body: Upstream body data\n   └─→ UpstreamRequest::decodeData() → Router → FilterManager::encodeData()\n   └─→ Encoder chain processes data\n   └─→ Codec encodes to wire\n\n8. Trailers and Completion\n   └─→ UpstreamRequest::decodeTrailers() → Router → FilterManager::encodeTrailers()\n   └─→ Downstream codec sends trailers\n   └─→ Stream marked complete\n\n9. Cleanup\n   └─→ ActiveStream marked for deferred deletion\n   └─→ Stream removed from connection manager's stream list\n   └─→ Upstream connection returned to pool\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nEnvoy provides several extension points where users can inject custom logic:\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\n**Interface:** `envoy::http::StreamFilter` (decoder + encoder) or `StreamDecoderFilter` / `StreamEncoderFilter`\n\n**Instantiation:** Via `FilterChainFactory` in HTTP connection manager configuration\n\n**Common patterns:**\n\n- **Authentication/Authorization**: Check credentials, modify headers\n- **Rate Limiting**: Enforce per-user or per-IP request limits\n- **Request/Response Transformation**: Modify headers, body, metadata\n- **Observability**: Extract metrics, trace spans\n- **Caching**: Return cached responses for GET requests\n\n**Example:** The router filter itself is instantiated as the terminal decoder filter via the standard factory mechanism.\n\n### 2. Cluster Extensions\n\n**Interfaces:**\n- `Cluster`: Load balancer factory, health checks, circuit breakers\n- `LoadBalancer`: Host selection algorithm\n- `HealthChecker`: Protocol-specific health check implementation\n\n**Extension points:**\n\n- **Load Balancer Implementations**: Custom algorithms (e.g., weighted round-robin with failures, geo-aware)\n- **Health Check Protocols**: Custom protocols beyond HTTP, TCP, gRPC\n- **Outlier Detection Algorithms**: Custom failure detection logic\n\n### 3. Route Configuration\n\n**Interface:** `RouteConfiguration` (typically from file or RDS)\n\n**Extension points:**\n\n- **Route matching**: Virtual hosts, path/method/header matching\n- **Cluster selection**: Static cluster, weighted clusters, header-based routing, regex path matching\n- **Per-route configuration**: Timeouts, retries, shadows, traffic policies\n\n### 4. Request/Response Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**Via FilterState and Callbacks:**\n\n- **FilterState**: Arbitrary key-value storage on `StreamInfo` for passing data between filters\n- **Access Logging**: Custom log sinks and formats\n- **Tracing**: Span creation and annotation at multiple stages\n\n### 5. Error Handling and Local Replies\n\nFilters can trigger local replies (responses generated by Envoy, not forwarded to upstream):\n\n```cpp\n// From any filter\nfilter_manager_.sendLocalReply(\n  Http::Code::Forbidden,\n  \"Access denied\",\n  modify_headers_fn,\n  grpc_status,\n  \"authz_denied\"\n);\n```\n\nThis allows:\n- **Early rejection** before routing\n- **Custom error responses** with appropriate status codes and bodies\n- **Request body discarding** (no upstream connection initiated)\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Codec Errors\n\nIf the incoming data is invalid HTTP:\n- The codec throws an exception or detects a protocol violation\n- ConnectionManager catches the error and issues a 400 Bad Request local reply\n- The connection may be closed (depending on severity)\n\n### Filter Errors\n\nIf a filter encounters an error:\n- It can issue a local reply via `sendLocalReply()`\n- This stops filter iteration and sends a response to the client\n- The upstream request (if any) is canceled\n\n### Upstream Failures\n\nSeveral upstream failure modes are handled:\n\n**Connection Failures:**\n- Router requests a pool; connection fails before headers sent\n- If retries remain, a new attempt is made to a different host\n- If retries exhausted, a local 503 (unavailable) or 504 (gateway timeout) reply is sent\n\n**Slow/Unresponsive Upstream:**\n- Per-try timeout is exceeded\n- Current upstream request is reset\n- New attempt initiated (if retries remain)\n- If hedging is enabled, secondary request may already be in flight\n\n**Upstream Reset/Protocol Violation:**\n- Upstream closes connection unexpectedly\n- Router detects the reset via `onResetStream()` callback\n- Request can be retried if safe (GET, HEAD, OPTIONS, etc.)\n\n**Response Too Large:**\n- FilterManager detects response body exceeds configured limit\n- Stream is reset with a local 413 Payload Too Large reply\n\n---\n\n## Request Flow Examples\n\n### Simple Request-Response\n\n```\nClient → [GET /api/users HTTP/1.1]\n  ↓\nConnectionManager::onData()\n  ↓\nCodec detects HTTP/1.1 request\n  ↓\nActiveStream created, FilterManager instantiated\n  ↓\nDecoder filters execute:\n  - Auth filter: validates credentials ✓\n  - Rate limit filter: checks quota ✓\n  - Router: selects route, gets pool to \"user-service\" cluster\n  ↓\nLoad balancer selects host 10.0.1.5:8080\n  ↓\nConnection pool returns connection\n  ↓\nUpstreamRequest forwards headers to upstream\n  ↓\nUpstream server processes, returns [200 OK, body: [...]]\n  ↓\nUpstreamRequest receives response headers\n  ↓\nEncoder filters execute:\n  - Router: processes upstream response\n  - Rate limit filter: records request ✓\n  - Auth filter: clears audit token ✓\n  ↓\nActiveStream encodes response to downstream\n  ↓\nClient receives response\n```\n\n### Request with Retry\n\n```\nClient → [POST /api/orders HTTP/1.1, body]\n  ↓\n... (decode headers through router filter)\n  ↓\nRouter obtains pool to \"order-service\"\n  ↓\nLoad balancer selects host 10.0.2.3:9000\n  ↓\nConnection pool: no connection available, create new\n  ↓\nConnection fails (port unreachable)\n  ↓\nonPoolFailure() invoked, retry count = 1\n  ↓\nRouter resets upstream request\n  ↓\nLoad balancer selects alternate host 10.0.2.4:9000\n  ↓\nConnection succeeds\n  ↓\nUpstreamRequest forwards headers/body/trailers\n  ↓\nUpstream responds [200 OK]\n  ↓\nResponse sent to client\n```\n\n### Filter-Generated Local Reply\n\n```\nClient → [GET /admin/config HTTP/1.1]\n  ↓\nActiveStream decodes headers\n  ↓\nAuth filter::decodeHeaders():\n  - Header: authorization: \"invalid-token\"\n  - Returns FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIteration\n  - Calls filter_manager_.sendLocalReply(401, \"Unauthorized\")\n  ↓\nFilterManager stops iteration, invokes encoder filters in reverse\n  ↓\nEncoder filters execute (for local reply):\n  - Auth filter\n  - Any before it\n  ↓\nCodec encodes response\n  ↓\nClient receives [401 Unauthorized]\n  ↓\nRequest body (if any) is discarded\n  ↓\nNo upstream connection initiated\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Source (Configuration)\n- **`api/envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto`**: v3 HCM configuration\n- **`api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/router/v3/router.proto`**: v3 Router filter configuration\n- **`api/envoy/config/route/v3/route.proto`**: Route configuration (virtual hosts, routes, clauses)\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager is a layered architecture that cleanly separates concerns:\n\n1. **Network Layer** (ConnectionManagerImpl): Owns connection lifecycle, codec instantiation, stream creation\n2. **Filter Chain Execution** (FilterManager): Orchestrates request/response processing through configurable filters\n3. **Routing and Forwarding** (Router Filter): Selects upstream targets and manages request forwarding\n4. **Upstream Connectivity** (ClusterManager): Manages connection pools, load balancing, health checking\n\nThis design enables:\n- **Protocol independence**: H1/H2/H3 handled through pluggable codecs\n- **Extensibility**: Filters can be inserted at any point without modifying core components\n- **Resilience**: Retries, timeouts, health checks, and circuit breakers protect against upstream failures\n- **Observability**: StreamInfo tracks request metadata; access logs and tracing integrate naturally\n- **Performance**: Lazy codec instantiation, connection pooling, and efficient filter iteration minimize overhead\n\nThe request flow is deterministic and well-ordered, enabling debugging, testing, and auditing of the request processing This document explains the architecture, data flow, and interaction patterns between the key components that make up this system.\n\nThe HCM operates at the network layer (as a `Network::ReadFilter`) and is protocol-agnostic—it transparently handles HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, and HTTP/3 through pluggable codec implementations. The request processing follows a well-defined pipeline: connection establishment → codec instantiation → per-stream filter chain execution → route selection → upstream forwarding.\n\n---\n\n## Component Responsibilities\n\n### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl\n\n**Location:** `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` and `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n\nConnectionManagerImpl is the central network filter that owns the lifecycle of an HTTP connection. It serves multiple interfaces simultaneously:\n\n- **Network::ReadFilter**: Receives raw bytes from the network\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks**: Creates new streams when the codec detects incoming requests\n- **Network::ConnectionCallbacks**: Handles connection-level events (connect, disconnect, watermarks)\n- **Http::ApiListener**: Allows programmatic creation of streams (used by gRPC transcoding, async clients)\n\n#### Codec Instantiation\n\nThe codec is created lazily:\n- For **H1/H2**: The codec is instantiated on the first `onData()` call via the `createCodec()` method, examining the incoming bytes to determine the protocol\n- For **H3**: The codec is created during `onNewConnection()` since the QUIC transport has already been established\n- The codec implements `ServerConnection`, which calls back to `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` when requests arrive\n\n#### Stream Management\n\nEach incoming HTTP request is wrapped in an `ActiveStream` structure, which:\n- Owns a `FilterManager` instance (the per-stream filter chain executor)\n- Tracks request/response headers, trailers, and stream state\n- Implements codec callbacks for low-level protocol events\n- Maintains `StreamInfo` for tracing, access logging, and runtime statistics\n- Is stored in a linked list (`LinkedObject<ActiveStream>`) for efficient iteration during shutdown\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : LinkedObject<ActiveStream>,\n                      public Event::DeferredDeletable,\n                      public StreamCallbacks,\n                      public CodecEventCallbacks,\n                      public RequestDecoder {\n  FilterManager filter_manager_;\n  RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr request_headers_;\n  ResponseHeaderMapPtr response_headers_;\n  ResponseTrailerMapPtr response_trailers_;\n  uint64_t stream_id_;\n  // ... additional state fields\n};\n```\n\n#### Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Drain Management**: When a drain decision is signaled (typically during graceful shutdown), the connection manager:\n1. Sets the codec to drain mode\n2. Stops accepting new requests\n3. Allows in-flight requests to complete\n4. Closes the connection after all streams are finished\n\n**Overload Management**: Integrates with the overload manager to:\n- Detect resource exhaustion (CPU, memory, connection saturation)\n- Send 503 Service Unavailable responses when overload thresholds are exceeded\n- Trigger connection draining under severe conditions\n\n**Watermark-Based Flow Control**:\n- Monitors the underlying connection's write buffer via `onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()` and `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`\n- Propagates watermark events to all active streams\n- Each stream notifies its filters to enable/disable reading from the request body\n\n---\n\n### 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain\n\n**Location:** `source/common/http/filter_manager.h` and `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n\nThe FilterManager is the per-stream execution engine for the HTTP filter chain. It orchestrates the passage of request headers, body data, and trailers through a chain of filters.\n\n#### Filter Chain Structure\n\nThe filter chain is asymmetric:\n\n**Decoder Filters (Request Path)**: Execute in configured order (A → B → C)\n- Receive `decodeHeaders()`, `decodeData()`, `decodeTrailers()`, `decodeMetadata()`\n- May stop iteration, buffer data, or modify headers\n- Responsible for forwarding to the next filter or local reply\n\n**Encoder Filters (Response Path)**: Execute in reverse order (C → B → A)\n- Receive `encode1xxHeaders()`, `encodeHeaders()`, `encodeData()`, `encodeTrailers()`, `encodeMetadata()`\n- Allow modification of response headers before sending to the client\n- This reverse order allows filters to apply transformations symmetrically\n\n```cpp\n// Decoder filters: forward iteration\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.begin(); }\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.end(); }\n};\n\n// Encoder filters: reverse iteration\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.rbegin(); }  // reverse begin\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.rend(); }      // reverse end\n};\n```\n\n#### Filter Lifecycle and Iteration Control\n\nEach filter wrapper (ActiveStreamDecoderFilter/ActiveStreamEncoderFilter) manages iteration state:\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStreamFilterBase {\n  enum class IterationState {\n    Continue,        // Continue to next filter\n    StopIteration,   // Stop, but continue processing later events\n    StopAllIteration // Buffer data, stop processing until conditions change\n  };\n\n  bool commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback(FilterHeadersStatus status, bool& end_stream);\n  bool commonHandleAfterDataCallback(FilterDataStatus status, Buffer::Instance& provided_data,\n                                     bool& buffer_was_streaming);\n};\n```\n\nWhen a filter returns:\n- **FilterHeadersStatus::Continue**: The next filter is invoked immediately\n- **FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration**: Iteration halts; the filter must explicitly call `continueDecoding()` or `continueEncoding()`\n- **FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIteration**: In addition to stopping iteration, data buffering is enabled\n\n#### Filter Chain Factory\n\nThe `FilterChainFactory` interface allows configuration of which filters are instantiated for each stream:\n\n```cpp\nclass FilterChainFactory {\npublic:\n  virtual void createFilterChain(FilterChainManager& manager) PURE;\n};\n```\n\nAt stream creation, the factory is invoked with the FilterManager to install decoder/encoder filters in the appropriate order. Filters are instantiated in order and may be:\n- **Decoder-only**: Implement `StreamDecoderFilter`\n- **Encoder-only**: Implement `StreamEncoderFilter`\n- **Dual filters**: Implement `StreamFilter` (both decoder and encoder)\n\n#### Local Reply Mechanism\n\nIf a filter (or any upstream component) detects an error, it can issue a local reply:\n\n```cpp\nfilter_manager_.sendLocalReply(\n  Http::Code::BadRequest,\n  \"Invalid header\",\n  [](ResponseHeaderMap& headers) { /* modify headers */ },\n  absl::nullopt,  // grpc_status\n  \"filter_validation_failed\"\n);\n```\n\nThe FilterManager:\n1. Stops further filter iteration\n2. Creates response headers (with the provided status code)\n3. Invokes encoder filters in reverse order\n4. Sends the response directly to the downstream codec\n5. Resets the stream\n\n---\n\n### 3. Router Filter\n\n**Location:** `source/common/router/router.h` and `source/common/router/router.cc`\n\nThe router filter is the **terminal decoder filter** in the standard HCM filter chain. Its responsibility is to:\n1. Select a route based on request properties\n2. Determine the target cluster/upstream service\n3. Create an `UpstreamRequest` and forward the request to the cluster manager\n4. Handle retries, timeouts, and upstream response processing\n\n#### Route Selection\n\nThe router uses the `RouteConfiguration` (obtained from the route provider) to match the incoming request:\n\n```cpp\n// From router_filter_interface.h\nclass Router {\n  virtual void setRoute(Router::RouteConstSharedPtr route) override {\n    // Cache the selected route\n  }\n};\n```\n\nRoute matching considers:\n- **Virtual hosts**: Hostname-based grouping of routes (from `:authority` header or SNI)\n- **Routes**: Ordered list of route entries matched by:\n  - Path prefix/regex\n  - Methods (GET, POST, etc.)\n  - Headers and header patterns\n  - Query parameters\n  - Traffic policy (canary, shadow)\n\nOnce a route is selected, the router extracts the **cluster name** from the route entry and queries the `ClusterManager` for an HTTP connection pool.\n\n#### Upstream Request Lifecycle\n\nWhen a route is selected, the router creates an `UpstreamRequest`:\n\n```cpp\nclass UpstreamRequest : public GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks,\n                        public UpstreamToDownstreamImplBase {\n  void acceptHeadersFromRouter(bool end_stream);\n  void acceptDataFromRouter(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\n  void onPoolReady(std::unique_ptr<GenericUpstream>&& upstream,\n                   Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host,\n                   const Network::ConnectionInfoProvider& address_provider,\n                   StreamInfo::StreamInfo& info,\n                   absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol) override;\n};\n```\n\nThe flow:\n\n1. **Request Pools**: The router calls `cluster_manager_->getPool()` passing:\n   - Cluster name\n   - Load balancing context (for host selection)\n   - Protocol preferences (H1, H2, H3)\n\n2. **Pool Acquisition**: The ClusterManager returns a connection pool. If no connection is available:\n   - **Pool Pending**: The UpstreamRequest's `onPoolReady()` callback is invoked once a connection is obtained\n   - **Pool Failure**: `onPoolFailure()` is invoked; the router issues a local reply with 503 or 504\n\n3. **Request Forwarding**: Once `onPoolReady()` is called with an upstream connection:\n   - An `UpstreamCodecFilter` is instantiated within an `UpstreamFilterManager`\n   - Request headers/body/trailers are forwarded to the upstream codec\n   - The upstream codec encodes and sends the request on the wire\n\n4. **Response Reception**: The upstream codec decodes response bytes and invokes:\n   - `decodeHeaders()`: Response status and headers\n   - `decodeData()`: Response body chunks\n   - `decodeTrailers()`: Optional trailers\n   - These flow backwards through the encoder filter chain to the downstream encoder\n\n#### Retry Logic\n\nThe router implements sophisticated retry handling via `RetryStateImpl`:\n\n```cpp\nclass RetryStateImpl {\n  void onUpstreamReset(Upstream::UpstreamResetReason reason);\n  bool shouldRetry(absl::optional<Http::Code> code, bool reset_reason_is_timeout);\n};\n```\n\nRetries are triggered by:\n- **Connection failures**: Pool timeout, connection refused, connection reset\n- **Specific response codes**: 5xx errors (configurable via retry policies)\n- **Timeout**: Per-try timeout exceeded\n\nConfiguration specifies:\n- Maximum retry count\n- Backoff policy (exponential with jitter)\n- Retriable response codes\n- Host selection strategy (use same host, alternate host)\n\n#### Timeout Management\n\nThe router maintains two timeout levels:\n\n- **Request timeout**: Total time allowed for the request (including retries)\n- **Per-try timeout**: Time limit for each individual attempt\n\nThese are set via:\n- Route configuration\n- `x-envoy-upstream-rq-timeout-ms` request header\n- `x-envoy-upstream-rq-per-try-timeout-ms` header\n\nWhen a timeout occurs:\n1. The current upstream request is reset\n2. If retries remain, a new attempt is initiated\n3. Otherwise, a 504 response is sent\n\n#### Hedged Requests (Per-Try Timeout)\n\nIf enabled, the router can initiate a secondary request before the primary completes:\n\n```cpp\n// When per_try_timeout triggers before the full request timeout:\n// 1. A new upstream request is started\n// 2. The first response to complete is used\n// 3. The slower request is abandoned\n```\n\n#### Shadow Routing\n\nThe router supports shadowing requests to a shadow cluster for testing:\n\n```cpp\nif (FilterUtility::shouldShadow(shadow_policy, runtime, stable_random)) {\n  auto shadow_request = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(...);\n  shadow_request->acceptHeadersFromRouter(end_stream);\n  // Response is silently discarded; no feedback to client\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n**Location:** `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h` and related files\n\nThe ClusterManager is the upstream connection pool and cluster management layer. It:\n1. Owns a registry of Cluster objects (one per configured cluster)\n2. Provides HTTP and TCP connection pools for each cluster\n3. Coordinates health checking and outlier detection\n4. Implements load balancing across hosts within a cluster\n\n#### ClusterManager Structure\n\n```cpp\nclass ClusterManagerImpl : public ClusterManager {\n  Cluster& cluster(const std::string& name);\n  Http::ConnectionPool::InstancePtr\n  getHttpConnectionPool(const ClusterConnectivityState& state,\n                        LoadBalancerContext* lb_context);\n};\n```\n\nEach `Cluster` object encapsulates:\n- A set of hosts/endpoints\n- A load balancer factory\n- Health checking configuration\n- Outlier detection rules\n- Circuit breaker limits\n\n#### Connection Pool Mechanics\n\nWhen the router requests a connection pool, the flow is:\n\n```\nRouter::getPool(cluster_name, load_balancing_context)\n  ↓\nClusterManager::getPool()\n  ↓\nCluster::getConnPool(dispatcher, load_balancer_context)\n  ↓\nConnectionPoolGrid::getPool()  [per-protocol instance]\n  ↓\nConnPoolBase::getHTTP1Connection() [if HTTP/1 pool requested]\n  ↓\n{\n  if (connection available and idle) {\n    return existing connection\n  } else if (connection limit not reached) {\n    create new connection and return\n  } else {\n    queue pending request\n  }\n}\n```\n\nA connection pool manages:\n- **Active connections**: Connections with in-flight requests\n- **Idle connections**: Connections available for reuse\n- **Pending requests**: Requests waiting for an available connection\n- **Watermark buffers**: Per-connection write buffers with high/low water marks\n\n#### Host Selection (Load Balancing)\n\nThe load balancer selects a specific host (endpoint) for each request:\n\n```cpp\nclass LoadBalancer {\n  HostConstSharedPtr chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext* context);\n};\n```\n\nThe router provides a `LoadBalancerContext` containing:\n- Request metadata (headers, cookies, etc.) for hash-based selection\n- Current retry count (for retry host selection)\n- Upstream zone information (for zone-aware routing)\n\nLoad balancing algorithms include:\n- **Round Robin**: Distribute evenly across healthy hosts\n- **Least Connections**: Select the host with fewest active connections\n- **Ring Hash**: Consistent hashing for session affinity\n- **Random**: Random selection\n- **Maglev**: Fast, deterministic hash with minimal disruption on host changes\n- **Locality-aware**: Prefer hosts in the same zone/region as the client\n\n#### Health Checking and Outlier Detection\n\n**Health Checking**: Periodic health checks (HTTP, TCP, gRPC) are configured per cluster:\n- Determines which hosts are available for traffic\n- Failed hosts are marked as unhealthy and excluded from load balancing\n- Recovered hosts are re-enabled\n\n**Outlier Detection**: Monitors request failures at runtime:\n- Tracks failure rates per host\n- Ejects hosts that exceed failure thresholds (e.g., >50% failure rate over 10 requests)\n- Periodically attempts to re-include ejected hosts\n- Provides fast, adaptive failure response (complementing health checks)\n\nBoth feed into the load balancer's host selection, ensuring traffic only reaches healthy hosts.\n\n#### Dynamic Cluster Discovery (CDS)\n\nClusters can be discovered dynamically via Cluster Discovery Service (CDS):\n\n```cpp\nclass CdsApi : public Config::SubscriptionCallbacks {\n  void onConfigUpdate(const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<ProtobufWkt::Any>& resources) override;\n};\n```\n\nCDS allows:\n- Adding new clusters without restarting\n- Updating cluster configuration (endpoints, health check policies)\n- Removing clusters gracefully\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Request Processing Pipeline\n\n### Downstream Request Path (Request Arrival to Upstream Dispatch)\n\n```\n1. Network Layer: Bytes arrive on downstream socket\n   └─→ ConnectionManager::onData(Buffer& data, bool end_stream)\n\n2. Codec Instantiation (first onData() call only)\n   └─→ ConnectionManager::createCodec()\n   └─→ HTTP1/2/3 CodecImpl selected\n   └─→ Codec parses protocol framing\n\n3. Stream Creation: Codec detects request headers\n   └─→ Codec::ServerConnection::newStream() callback\n   └─→ ConnectionManager::newStream(ResponseEncoder& response_encoder)\n   └─→ Creates ActiveStream with FilterManager\n\n4. Request Decoding: Codec delivers framing events\n   └─→ ActiveStream::decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream)\n   └─→ FilterManager::decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)\n\n5. Filter Chain Execution (Decoder Path): A → B → C\n   ├─→ FilterA::decodeHeaders() → returns Continue\n   ├─→ FilterB::decodeHeaders() → returns Continue\n   ├─→ RouterFilter::decodeHeaders()\n   │   ├─→ Route selection (virtual host + route matching)\n   │   ├─→ Cluster selection from route\n   │   └─→ ClusterManager::getPool(cluster_name, lb_context)\n   │\n   └─→ Pool resolution callback invoked (synchronous or deferred)\n       ├─→ Host selection via load balancer\n       ├─→ Connection pool creates/reuses connection to host\n       └─→ UpstreamRequest created\n\n6. Body Data Processing: If request has body\n   └─→ ActiveStream::decodeData(Buffer& data, bool end_stream)\n   └─→ FilterManager::decodeData(data, end_stream)\n   └─→ Filters iterate in order (A → B → Router)\n   └─→ Router accumulates or forwards to upstream via UpstreamRequest\n\n7. Trailers Processing: If request has trailers\n   └─→ ActiveStream::decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMap& trailers)\n   └─→ FilterManager::decodeTrailers(trailers)\n   └─→ Filters iterate in order\n   └─→ Router forwards to upstream\n\n8. Upstream Request Forwarding (UpstreamRequest)\n   └─→ UpstreamCodecFilter encodes headers/data/trailers\n   └─→ Codec writes to upstream connection\n   └─→ Request transmitted on wire\n```\n\n### Upstream Response Path (Response Reception to Downstream Delivery)\n\n```\n1. Upstream Response: Bytes received on upstream socket\n   └─→ Upstream codec parses HTTP framing\n\n2. Response Decoding: Codec detects response headers\n   └─→ Codec::ResponseDecoder::decode1xxHeaders() / decodeHeaders()\n   └─→ UpstreamCodecFilter receives via CodecBridge\n   └─→ UpstreamFilterManager::encodeHeaders() [confusingly named]\n\n3. Upstream Filter Chain: Encoder filters (reverse order C → B → A)\n   └─→ Allow modification of response before sending to client\n\n4. Response Delivery to Router Filter\n   └─→ UpstreamRequest::decode1xxHeaders() / decodeHeaders() [legacy API]\n   └─→ Router notifies downstream filter chain via\n       RouterFilterInterface::onUpstream1xxHeaders() / onUpstreamHeaders()\n\n5. Response Encoding: Router injects response into downstream encoder chain\n   └─→ FilterManager::encodeHeaders() [actual encoding operation]\n   └─→ Encoder filters iterate in reverse (C → B → A)\n   └─→ Each filter may modify response headers\n\n6. Codec Encoding: Final encoder (ConnectionManager's codec)\n   └─→ ActiveStream::encodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream)\n   └─→ Codec encodes headers into wire format\n\n7. Response Body: Upstream body data\n   └─→ UpstreamRequest::decodeData() → Router → FilterManager::encodeData()\n   └─→ Encoder chain processes data\n   └─→ Codec encodes to wire\n\n8. Trailers and Completion\n   └─→ UpstreamRequest::decodeTrailers() → Router → FilterManager::encodeTrailers()\n   └─→ Downstream codec sends trailers\n   └─→ Stream marked complete\n\n9. Cleanup\n   └─→ ActiveStream marked for deferred deletion\n   └─→ Stream removed from connection manager's stream list\n   └─→ Upstream connection returned to pool\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nEnvoy provides several extension points where users can inject custom logic:\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\n**Interface:** `envoy::http::StreamFilter` (decoder + encoder) or `StreamDecoderFilter` / `StreamEncoderFilter`\n\n**Instantiation:** Via `FilterChainFactory` in HTTP connection manager configuration\n\n**Common patterns:**\n\n- **Authentication/Authorization**: Check credentials, modify headers\n- **Rate Limiting**: Enforce per-user or per-IP request limits\n- **Request/Response Transformation**: Modify headers, body, metadata\n- **Observability**: Extract metrics, trace spans\n- **Caching**: Return cached responses for GET requests\n\n**Example:** The router filter itself is instantiated as the terminal decoder filter via the standard factory mechanism.\n\n### 2. Cluster Extensions\n\n**Interfaces:**\n- `Cluster`: Load balancer factory, health checks, circuit breakers\n- `LoadBalancer`: Host selection algorithm\n- `HealthChecker`: Protocol-specific health check implementation\n\n**Extension points:**\n\n- **Load Balancer Implementations**: Custom algorithms (e.g., weighted round-robin with failures, geo-aware)\n- **Health Check Protocols**: Custom protocols beyond HTTP, TCP, gRPC\n- **Outlier Detection Algorithms**: Custom failure detection logic\n\n### 3. Route Configuration\n\n**Interface:** `RouteConfiguration` (typically from file or RDS)\n\n**Extension points:**\n\n- **Route matching**: Virtual hosts, path/method/header matching\n- **Cluster selection**: Static cluster, weighted clusters, header-based routing, regex path matching\n- **Per-route configuration**: Timeouts, retries, shadows, traffic policies\n\n### 4. Request/Response Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**Via FilterState and Callbacks:**\n\n- **FilterState**: Arbitrary key-value storage on `StreamInfo` for passing data between filters\n- **Access Logging**: Custom log sinks and formats\n- **Tracing**: Span creation and annotation at multiple stages\n\n### 5. Error Handling and Local Replies\n\nFilters can trigger local replies (responses generated by Envoy, not forwarded to upstream):\n\n```cpp\n// From any filter\nfilter_manager_.sendLocalReply(\n  Http::Code::Forbidden,\n  \"Access denied\",\n  modify_headers_fn,\n  grpc_status,\n  \"authz_denied\"\n);\n```\n\nThis allows:\n- **Early rejection** before routing\n- **Custom error responses** with appropriate status codes and bodies\n- **Request body discarding** (no upstream connection initiated)\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Codec Errors\n\nIf the incoming data is invalid HTTP:\n- The codec throws an exception or detects a protocol violation\n- ConnectionManager catches the error and issues a 400 Bad Request local reply\n- The connection may be closed (depending on severity)\n\n### Filter Errors\n\nIf a filter encounters an error:\n- It can issue a local reply via `sendLocalReply()`\n- This stops filter iteration and sends a response to the client\n- The upstream request (if any) is canceled\n\n### Upstream Failures\n\nSeveral upstream failure modes are handled:\n\n**Connection Failures:**\n- Router requests a pool; connection fails before headers sent\n- If retries remain, a new attempt is made to a different host\n- If retries exhausted, a local 503 (unavailable) or 504 (gateway timeout) reply is sent\n\n**Slow/Unresponsive Upstream:**\n- Per-try timeout is exceeded\n- Current upstream request is reset\n- New attempt initiated (if retries remain)\n- If hedging is enabled, secondary request may already be in flight\n\n**Upstream Reset/Protocol Violation:**\n- Upstream closes connection unexpectedly\n- Router detects the reset via `onResetStream()` callback\n- Request can be retried if safe (GET, HEAD, OPTIONS, etc.)\n\n**Response Too Large:**\n- FilterManager detects response body exceeds configured limit\n- Stream is reset with a local 413 Payload Too Large reply\n\n---\n\n## Request Flow Examples\n\n### Simple Request-Response\n\n```\nClient → [GET /api/users HTTP/1.1]\n  ↓\nConnectionManager::onData()\n  ↓\nCodec detects HTTP/1.1 request\n  ↓\nActiveStream created, FilterManager instantiated\n  ↓\nDecoder filters execute:\n  - Auth filter: validates credentials ✓\n  - Rate limit filter: checks quota ✓\n  - Router: selects route, gets pool to \"user-service\" cluster\n  ↓\nLoad balancer selects host 10.0.1.5:8080\n  ↓\nConnection pool returns connection\n  ↓\nUpstreamRequest forwards headers to upstream\n  ↓\nUpstream server processes, returns [200 OK, body: [...]]\n  ↓\nUpstreamRequest receives response headers\n  ↓\nEncoder filters execute:\n  - Router: processes upstream response\n  - Rate limit filter: records request ✓\n  - Auth filter: clears audit token ✓\n  ↓\nActiveStream encodes response to downstream\n  ↓\nClient receives response\n```\n\n### Request with Retry\n\n```\nClient → [POST /api/orders HTTP/1.1, body]\n  ↓\n... (decode headers through router filter)\n  ↓\nRouter obtains pool to \"order-service\"\n  ↓\nLoad balancer selects host 10.0.2.3:9000\n  ↓\nConnection pool: no connection available, create new\n  ↓\nConnection fails (port unreachable)\n  ↓\nonPoolFailure() invoked, retry count = 1\n  ↓\nRouter resets upstream request\n  ↓\nLoad balancer selects alternate host 10.0.2.4:9000\n  ↓\nConnection succeeds\n  ↓\nUpstreamRequest forwards headers/body/trailers\n  ↓\nUpstream responds [200 OK]\n  ↓\nResponse sent to client\n```\n\n### Filter-Generated Local Reply\n\n```\nClient → [GET /admin/config HTTP/1.1]\n  ↓\nActiveStream decodes headers\n  ↓\nAuth filter::decodeHeaders():\n  - Header: authorization: \"invalid-token\"\n  - Returns FilterHeadersStatus::StopAllIteration\n  - Calls filter_manager_.sendLocalReply(401, \"Unauthorized\")\n  ↓\nFilterManager stops iteration, invokes encoder filters in reverse\n  ↓\nEncoder filters execute (for local reply):\n  - Auth filter\n  - Any before it\n  ↓\nCodec encodes response\n  ↓\nClient receives [401 Unauthorized]\n  ↓\nRequest body (if any) is discarded\n  ↓\nNo upstream connection initiated\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Source clauses)\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager is a layered architecture that cleanly separates concerns:\n\n1. **Network Layer** (ConnectionManagerImpl): Owns connection lifecycle, codec instantiation, stream creation\n2. **Filter Chain Execution** (FilterManager): Orchestrates request/response processing through configurable filters\n3. **Routing and Forwarding** (Router Filter): Selects upstream targets and manages request forwarding\n4. **Upstream Connectivity** (ClusterManager): Manages connection pools, load balancing, health checking\n\nThis design enables:\n- **Protocol independence**: H1/H2/H3 handled through pluggable codecs\n- **Extensibility**: Filters can be inserted at any point without modifying core components\n- **Resilience**: Retries, timeouts, health checks, and circuit breakers protect against upstream failures\n- **Observability**: StreamInfo tracks request metadata; access logs and tracing integrate naturally\n- **Performance**: Lazy codec instantiation, connection pooling, and efficient filter iteration minimize overhead\n\nThe request flow is deterministic and well-ordered, enabling debugging, testing, and auditing of the request processing pipeline.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
